<li value="1">These are the titles as given in the <i>Constitution of the Republic of Cameroon</i>, Article X (<a class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20060228030033/http://confinder.richmond.edu/admin/docs/Cameroon.pdf" rel="nofollow">English</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Wayback_Machine" title="Wayback Machine">Wayback Machine</a> (archived 28 February 2006) and <a class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20060228030033/http://www.prc.cm/instit/consti.htm" rel="nofollow">French</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Wayback_Machine" title="Wayback Machine">Wayback Machine</a> (archived 28 February 2006) versions). 18 January 1996. The French version of the song is sometimes called <i lang="fr" title="French language text">Chant de Ralliement</i>, as in Swarovski Orchestra (2004). <i>National Anthems of the World</i>. Koch International Classics; and the English version "O Cameroon, Cradle of Our Forefathers", as in <a href="#DeLancey">DeLancey and DeLancey</a> 61.</li>
</ol></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p><b>Cameroon</b> (<span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="'k' in 'kind'">k</span><span title="/æ/: 'a' in 'bad'">æ</span><span title="'m' in 'my'">m</span><span title="/ə/: 'a' in 'about'">ə</span><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'r' in 'rye'">r</span><span title="/uː/: 'oo' in 'goose'">uː</span><span title="'n' in 'nigh'">n</span></span>/</a></span><small class="nowrap"> (<span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap"><a href="/wiki/File:En-Cameroon-pronunciation.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="About this sound" data-file-height="20" data-file-width="20" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" width="11"/></a> </span><a class="internal" href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/f/f1/En-Cameroon-pronunciation.ogg" title="En-Cameroon-pronunciation.ogg">listen</a></span></span>)</small></span>; <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a>: <i lang="fr">Cameroun</i>), officially the <b>Republic of Cameroon</b> (French: <i lang="fr">République du Cameroun</i>), is a country wedged in West and Central Africa. It is bordered by <a href="/wiki/Nigeria" title="Nigeria">Nigeria</a> to the west and north; <a href="/wiki/Chad" title="Chad">Chad</a> to the northeast; the <a href="/wiki/Central_African_Republic" title="Central African Republic">Central African Republic</a> to the east; and <a href="/wiki/Equatorial_Guinea" title="Equatorial Guinea">Equatorial Guinea</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gabon" title="Gabon">Gabon</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Republic of the Congo">Republic of the Congo</a> to the south. Cameroon's coastline lies on the <a href="/wiki/Bight_of_Biafra" title="Bight of Biafra">Bight of Biafra</a>, part of the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Guinea" title="Gulf of Guinea">Gulf of Guinea</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Ocean" title="Atlantic Ocean">Atlantic Ocean</a>. Although Cameroon is not an ECOWAS member state, it geographically and historically is in West Africa with the <a href="/wiki/Southern_Cameroons" title="Southern Cameroons">Southern Cameroons</a> which now form her <a href="/wiki/Northwest_Region_(Cameroon)" title="Northwest Region (Cameroon)">Northwest</a> and <a href="/wiki/Southwest_Region_(Cameroon)" title="Southwest Region (Cameroon)">Southwest</a> Regions having a strong West African history. The country is sometimes identified as West African and other times as Central African due to its strategic position at the crossroads between West and Central Africa.
</p><p>French and English are the official languages of Cameroon. The country is often referred to as "Africa in miniature" for its geological and cultural diversity. Natural features include <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Beaches" title="Beaches">beaches</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Deserts" title="Deserts">deserts</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mountains" title="Mountains">mountains</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rainforests" title="Rainforests">rainforests</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Savannas" title="Savannas">savannas</a>. The highest point at almost 4,100 metres (13,500 ft) is <a href="/wiki/Mount_Cameroon" title="Mount Cameroon">Mount Cameroon</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Southwest_Region_(Cameroon)" title="Southwest Region (Cameroon)">Southwest Region</a> of the country, and the largest cities in population-terms are <a href="/wiki/Douala" title="Douala">Douala</a> on the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wouri_river" title="Wouri river">Wouri river</a>, its economic capital and main seaport, <a href="/wiki/Yaound%C3%A9" title="Yaoundé">Yaoundé</a>, its political capital, and <a href="/wiki/Garoua" title="Garoua">Garoua</a>. The country is well known for its native styles of music, particularly <a href="/wiki/Makossa" title="Makossa">makossa</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bikutsi" title="Bikutsi">bikutsi</a>, and for its successful <a href="/wiki/Cameroon_national_football_team" title="Cameroon national football team">national football team</a>.
</p><p>Early inhabitants of the territory included the <a href="/wiki/Sao_civilisation" title="Sao civilisation">Sao civilisation</a> around <a href="/wiki/Lake_Chad" title="Lake Chad">Lake Chad</a> and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Baka_(Cameroon_and_Gabon)" title="Baka (Cameroon and Gabon)">Baka</a> hunter-gatherers in the southeastern rainforest. <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_discoveries" title="Portuguese discoveries">Portuguese explorers</a> reached the coast in the 15th century and named the area <i>Rio dos Camarões</i> (<i>Shrimp River</i>), which became <i>Cameroon</i> in English. <a href="/wiki/Fula_people" title="Fula people">Fulani</a> soldiers founded the <a href="/wiki/Adamawa_Emirate" title="Adamawa Emirate">Adamawa Emirate</a> in the north in the 19th century, and various ethnic groups of the west and northwest established powerful chiefdoms and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fon_(Cameroon)" title="Fon (Cameroon)">fondoms</a>. Cameroon became a <a href="/wiki/German_Empire" title="German Empire">German colony</a> in 1884 known as <a href="/wiki/Kamerun" title="Kamerun">Kamerun</a>.
</p><p>After <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a>, the territory was divided between <a href="/wiki/French_Third_Republic" title="French Third Republic">France</a> and the <a href="/wiki/British_Empire" title="British Empire">United Kingdom</a> as <a href="/wiki/League_of_Nations_mandate" title="League of Nations mandate">League of Nations mandates</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Union_of_the_Peoples_of_Cameroon" title="Union of the Peoples of Cameroon">Union des Populations du Cameroun</a> (UPC) political party advocated independence, but was outlawed by France in the 1950s, leading to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cameroonian_Independence_War" title="Cameroonian Independence War">Cameroonian Independence War</a> fought between French and UPC militant forces until early 1971. In 1960, the French-administered part of Cameroon became independent as the Republic of Cameroun under President <a href="/wiki/Ahmadou_Ahidjo" title="Ahmadou Ahidjo">Ahmadou Ahidjo</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Southern_Cameroons" title="Southern Cameroons">southern part</a> of <a href="/wiki/British_Cameroons" title="British Cameroons">British Cameroons</a> federated with it in 1961 to form the <a href="/wiki/Federal_republic" title="Federal republic">Federal Republic</a> of Cameroon. The federation was abandoned in 1972. The country was renamed the <a href="/wiki/Unitary_state" title="Unitary state">United Republic</a> of Cameroon in 1972 and the Republic of Cameroon in 1984. Cameroon experiences relatively high political and social stability. This has permitted the development of agriculture, roads, railways and large petroleum and timber industries. Large numbers of Cameroonians live as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Subsistence_farmers" title="Subsistence farmers">subsistence farmers</a>. Since 1982 <a href="/wiki/Paul_Biya" title="Paul Biya">Paul Biya</a> has been President, governing with his <a href="/wiki/Cameroon_People%27s_Democratic_Movement" title="Cameroon People's Democratic Movement">Cameroon People's Democratic Movement</a> party. The country has experienced tensions coming from the English-speaking territories. Politicians in the English-speaking regions have advocated for greater decentralisation and even complete separation or independence (as in the <a href="/wiki/Southern_Cameroons_National_Council" title="Southern Cameroons National Council">Southern Cameroons National Council</a>) from Cameroon.
</p>
