<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cameroon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Cameroon" title="History of Cameroon">History of Cameroon</a></div>
<p>The territory of present-day Cameroon was first settled during the <a href="/wiki/Neolithic" title="Neolithic">Neolithic</a> Era. The longest continuous inhabitants are groups such as the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Baka_(Cameroon_and_Gabon)" title="Baka (Cameroon and Gabon)">Baka</a> (<a href="/wiki/Pygmy_peoples" title="Pygmy peoples">Pygmies</a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup> From here, <a href="/wiki/Bantu_expansion" title="Bantu expansion">Bantu migrations</a> into eastern, southern, and central Africa are believed to have originated about 2,000 years ago.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-history_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-history-9">[9]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Sao_civilisation" title="Sao civilisation">Sao</a> culture arose around <a href="/wiki/Lake_Chad" title="Lake Chad">Lake Chad</a> c. AD 500 and gave way to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kanem_Empire" title="Kanem Empire">Kanem</a> and its successor state, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bornu_Empire" title="Bornu Empire">Bornu Empire</a>. Kingdoms, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fon_(Cameroon)" title="Fon (Cameroon)">fondoms</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Chiefdom" title="Chiefdom">chiefdoms</a> arose in the west.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Njung_10-0"><a href="#cite_note-Njung-10">[10]</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Portuguese_discoveries" title="Portuguese discoveries">Portuguese sailors</a> reached the coast in 1472. They noted an abundance of the ghost shrimp <i><a href="/wiki/Lepidophthalmus_turneranus" title="Lepidophthalmus turneranus">Lepidophthalmus turneranus</a></i> in the <a href="/wiki/Wouri_River" title="Wouri River">Wouri River</a> and named it <i lang="pt" title="Portuguese language text">Rio dos Camarões</i> (<i>Shrimp River</i>), which became <i>Cameroon</i> in English.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup> Over the following few centuries, European interests regularised trade with the coastal peoples, and Christian <a href="/wiki/Missionary" title="Missionary">missionaries</a> pushed inland.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Fanso_12-0"><a href="#cite_note-Fanso-12">[12]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="The_1800s">The 1800s</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cameroon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: The 1800s">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Shumom-text.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="478" data-file-width="371" height="283" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Shumom-text.jpg/220px-Shumom-text.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Shumom-text.jpg/330px-Shumom-text.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/d/dc/Shumom-text.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Shumom-text.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Bamum_script" title="Bamum script">Bamum script</a> is a writing system developed by King Njoya in the late 19th century</div></div></div>
<p>In the early 19th century, <a href="/wiki/Modibo_Adama" title="Modibo Adama">Modibo Adama</a> led <a href="/wiki/Fula_people" title="Fula people">Fulani</a> soldiers on a <a href="/wiki/Jihad" title="Jihad">jihad</a> in the north against non-Muslim and partially Muslim peoples and established the <a href="/wiki/Adamawa_Emirate" title="Adamawa Emirate">Adamawa Emirate</a>. Settled peoples who fled the Fulani caused a major redistribution of population.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Fanso_12-1"><a href="#cite_note-Fanso-12">[12]</a></sup> The northern part of Cameroon was an important part of the <a href="/wiki/Arab_slave_trade" title="Arab slave trade">Arab slave trade</a> network.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-history_9-1"><a href="#cite_note-history-9">[9]</a></sup>
</p><p>The Bamum tribe have a writing system, known as <a href="/wiki/Bamum_script" title="Bamum script">Bamum script</a> or Shu Mom. The script was given to them by Sultan <a href="/wiki/Ibrahim_Njoya" title="Ibrahim Njoya">Ibrahim Njoya</a> in 1896,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NMAA_14-0"><a href="#cite_note-NMAA-14">[14]</a></sup> and is taught in Cameroon by the <a href="/wiki/Bamum_Scripts_and_Archives_Project" title="Bamum Scripts and Archives Project">Bamum Scripts and Archives Project</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NMAA_14-1"><a href="#cite_note-NMAA-14">[14]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">Germany</a> began to establish roots in Cameroon in 1868 when the Woermann Company of Hamburg built a warehouse. It was built on the estuary of the Wouri River. Later Gustav Nachtigal made a treaty with one of the local kings to annex the region for the German emperor.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-historyworld_15-0"><a href="#cite_note-historyworld-15">[15]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/German_Empire" title="German Empire">German Empire</a> claimed the territory as the colony of <a href="/wiki/Kamerun" title="Kamerun">Kamerun</a> in 1884 and began a steady push inland. The Germans ran into resistance with the native people who did not want the Germans to establish themselves on this land. Under the influence of Germany, commercial companies were left to regulate local administrations. These concessions used forced labour of the Africans to make a profit. The labour was used on banana, rubber, palm oil, and cocoa plantations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-historyworld_15-1"><a href="#cite_note-historyworld-15">[15]</a></sup> They initiated projects to improve the colony's infrastructure, relying on a harsh system of <a href="/wiki/Unfree_labour" title="Unfree labour">forced labour</a>, which was much criticised by the other colonial powers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DeLancey_125_16-0"><a href="#cite_note-DeLancey_125-16">[16]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="The_1900s">The 1900s</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cameroon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: The 1900s">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>With the defeat of Germany in <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a>, Kamerun became a <a href="/wiki/League_of_Nations_mandate" title="League of Nations mandate">League of Nations mandate</a> territory and was split into <a href="/wiki/French_Cameroons" title="French Cameroons">French Cameroons</a> and <a href="/wiki/British_Cameroons" title="British Cameroons">British Cameroons</a> in 1919. France integrated the economy of Cameroon with that of France<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DeLancey_5_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-DeLancey_5-17">[17]</a></sup> and improved the infrastructure with capital investments and skilled workers, modifying the system of forced labour.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DeLancey_125_16-1"><a href="#cite_note-DeLancey_125-16">[16]</a></sup>
</p><p>The British administered their territory from neighbouring <a href="/wiki/Nigeria" title="Nigeria">Nigeria</a>. Natives complained that this made them a neglected "colony of a colony". Nigerian migrant workers flocked to Southern Cameroons, ending forced labour altogether but angering the local natives, who felt swamped.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup> The League of Nations mandates were converted into <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Trusteeship_Council" title="United Nations Trusteeship Council">United Nations Trusteeships</a> in 1946, and the question of independence became a pressing issue in French Cameroun.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DeLancey_5_17-1"><a href="#cite_note-DeLancey_5-17">[17]</a></sup>
</p><p>France outlawed the most radical political party, the <a href="/wiki/Union_of_the_Peoples_of_Cameroon" title="Union of the Peoples of Cameroon">Union des Populations du Cameroun</a> (UPC), on 13 July 1955.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup> This prompted a long guerrilla war and the assassination of the party's leader, <a href="/wiki/Ruben_Um_Nyob%C3%A9" title="Ruben Um Nyobé">Ruben Um Nyobé</a>. In the more peaceful British Cameroons, the question was whether to reunify with French Cameroun or join Nigeria.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span id="Independence_.281960.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Independence_(1960)">Independence (1960)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cameroon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Independence (1960)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:166px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ahmadou_Ahidjo.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="211" data-file-width="164" height="211" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/d/db/Ahmadou_Ahidjo.jpg" width="164"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ahmadou_Ahidjo.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Former president <a href="/wiki/Ahmadou_Ahidjo" title="Ahmadou Ahidjo">Ahmadou Ahidjo</a> ruled from 1960 until 1982.</div></div></div>
<p>On 1 January 1960, French Cameroun gained independence from France under President <a href="/wiki/Ahmadou_Ahidjo" title="Ahmadou Ahidjo">Ahmadou Ahidjo</a>. On 1 October 1961, the formerly British <a href="/wiki/Southern_Cameroons" title="Southern Cameroons">Southern Cameroons</a> united with French Cameroun to form the Federal Republic of Cameroon. Ahidjo used the ongoing war with the UPC to concentrate power in the presidency, continuing with this even after the suppression of the UPC in 1971.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DeLancey_6_21-0"><a href="#cite_note-DeLancey_6-21">[21]</a></sup>
</p><p>His political party, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cameroon_National_Union" title="Cameroon National Union">Cameroon National Union</a> (CNU), became the sole legal political party on 1 September 1966 and in 1972, the <a href="/wiki/Federation" title="Federation">federal system of government</a> was abolished in favour of a United Republic of Cameroon, headed from <a href="/wiki/Yaound%C3%A9" title="Yaoundé">Yaoundé</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup> Ahidjo pursued an economic policy of <a href="/wiki/Planned_liberalism" title="Planned liberalism">planned liberalism</a>, prioritising <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cash_crops" title="Cash crops">cash crops</a> and petroleum development. The government used oil money to create a national cash reserve, pay farmers, and finance major development projects; however, many initiatives failed when Ahidjo appointed unqualified allies to direct them.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Paul_Biya_2014.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="617" data-file-width="517" height="263" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Paul_Biya_2014.png/220px-Paul_Biya_2014.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Paul_Biya_2014.png/330px-Paul_Biya_2014.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Paul_Biya_2014.png/440px-Paul_Biya_2014.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Paul_Biya_2014.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Paul_Biya" title="Paul Biya">Paul Biya</a> has ruled the country since 1982</div></div></div>
<p>Ahidjo stepped down on 4 November 1982 and left power to his constitutional successor, <a href="/wiki/Paul_Biya" title="Paul Biya">Paul Biya</a>. However, Ahidjo remained in control of the CNU and tried to run the country from behind the scenes until Biya and his allies pressured him into resigning. Biya began his administration by moving toward a more democratic government, but a failed <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cameroonian_Palace_Guard_Revolt" title="Cameroonian Palace Guard Revolt">coup d'état</a> nudged him toward the leadership style of his predecessor.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup>
</p><p>An <a href="/wiki/Economic_crisis_of_Cameroon" title="Economic crisis of Cameroon">economic crisis</a> took effect in the mid-1980s to late 1990s as a result of international economic conditions, drought, falling <a href="/wiki/Petroleum" title="Petroleum">petroleum</a> prices, and years of corruption, mismanagement, and <a href="/wiki/Cronyism" title="Cronyism">cronyism</a>. Cameroon turned to foreign aid, cut government spending, and <a href="/wiki/Privatization" title="Privatization">privatised</a> industries. With the reintroduction of multi-party politics in December 1990, the former British Southern Cameroons pressure groups called for greater autonomy, and the <a href="/wiki/Southern_Cameroons_National_Council" title="Southern Cameroons National Council">Southern Cameroons National Council</a> advocated complete secession as the Republic of <a href="/wiki/Ambazonia" title="Ambazonia">Ambazonia</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DeLancey_9_25-0"><a href="#cite_note-DeLancey_9-25">[25]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="21st_century">21st century</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cameroon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: 21st century">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In June 2006, talks concerning a territorial dispute over the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bakassi_peninsula" title="Bakassi peninsula">Bakassi peninsula</a> were resolved. The talks involved President Paul Biya of Cameroon, then President <a href="/wiki/Olusegun_Obasanjo" title="Olusegun Obasanjo">Olusegun Obasanjo</a> of Nigeria and then UN Secretary General <a href="/wiki/Kofi_Annan" title="Kofi Annan">Kofi Annan</a>, and resulted in Cameroonian control of the oil-rich peninsula. The northern portion of the territory was formally handed over to the Cameroonian government in August 2006, and the remainder of the peninsula was left to Cameroon 2 years later, in 2008.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup>
</p><p>In February 2008, Cameroon experienced its worst violence in 15 years when a transport union strike in Douala escalated into <a href="/wiki/2008_Cameroonian_anti-government_protests" title="2008 Cameroonian anti-government protests">violent protests</a> in 31 municipal areas.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Nkemngu_27-0"><a href="#cite_note-Nkemngu-27">[27]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Matthews_28-0"><a href="#cite_note-Matthews-28">[28]</a></sup>
</p><p>In May 2014, in the wake of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chibok_schoolgirl_kidnapping" title="Chibok schoolgirl kidnapping">Chibok schoolgirl kidnapping</a>, presidents Paul Biya of Cameroon and <a href="/wiki/Idriss_D%C3%A9by" title="Idriss Déby">Idriss Déby</a> of <a href="/wiki/Chad" title="Chad">Chad</a> announced they are waging war on <a href="/wiki/Boko_Haram" title="Boko Haram">Boko Haram</a>, and deployed troops to the Nigerian border.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup><br/>
</p><p>Since November 2016, protesters from the predominantly English-speaking <a href="/wiki/Northwest_Region_(Cameroon)" title="Northwest Region (Cameroon)">Northwest</a> and <a href="/wiki/Southwest_Region_(Cameroon)" title="Southwest Region (Cameroon)">Southwest</a> regions of the country have been campaigning for continued use of the English language in schools and courts. People were killed and hundreds jailed as a result of these protests.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup> In 2017, Biya's government blocked the regions' access to the Internet for three months.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup> As of  2018<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Cameroon&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, fighting between separatist militants and government forces continues.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Politics_and_government">Politics and government</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cameroon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Politics and government">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:YaoundeUnityPalace.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="399" data-file-width="605" height="198" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/YaoundeUnityPalace.png/300px-YaoundeUnityPalace.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/YaoundeUnityPalace.png/450px-YaoundeUnityPalace.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/YaoundeUnityPalace.png/600px-YaoundeUnityPalace.png 2x" width="300"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:YaoundeUnityPalace.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Unity Palace – Cameroon Presidency.</div></div></div>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Cameroon" title="Politics of Cameroon">Politics of Cameroon</a></div>
<p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Heads_of_state_of_Cameroon" title="Heads of state of Cameroon">President of Cameroon</a> is elected and creates policy, administers government agencies, commands the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Military_of_Cameroon" title="Military of Cameroon">armed forces</a>, negotiates and ratifies treaties, and declares a state of emergency.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Neba_250_33-0"><a href="#cite_note-Neba_250-33">[33]</a></sup> The president appoints government officials at all levels, from the <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Cameroon" title="Prime Minister of Cameroon">prime minister</a> (considered the official head of government), to the provincial governors and divisional officers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-msu_34-0"><a href="#cite_note-msu-34">[34]</a></sup> The president is selected by popular vote every seven years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CIA_1-2"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-1">[1]</a></sup> There have been 2 presidents since the independence of Cameroon.
</p><p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/National_Assembly_of_Cameroon" title="National Assembly of Cameroon">National Assembly</a> makes legislation. The body consists of 180 members who are elected for five-year terms and meet three times per year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-msu_34-1"><a href="#cite_note-msu-34">[34]</a></sup> Laws are passed on a majority vote. Rarely has the assembly changed or blocked legislation proposed by the president.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CIA_1-3"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-1">[1]</a></sup>
</p><p>The 1996 constitution establishes a second house of parliament, the 100-seat <a href="/wiki/Senate_(Cameroon)" title="Senate (Cameroon)">Senate</a>, was established in April 2013 and is headed by a President of the Senate who is the constitutional successor in case of untimely vacancy of the Presidency of the Republic.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CIA_1-4"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-1">[1]</a></sup> The government recognises the authority of traditional chiefs, fons, and <a href="/wiki/Lamido" title="Lamido">lamibe</a> to govern at the local level and to resolve disputes as long as such rulings do not conflict with national law.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-State_Dept_35-0"><a href="#cite_note-State_Dept-35">[35]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup>
</p><p>Cameroon's legal system is largely based on <a href="/wiki/Law_of_France" title="Law of France">French civil law</a> with common law influences.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CIA_1-5"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-1">[1]</a></sup> Although nominally independent, the judiciary falls under the authority of the executive's <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Justice_of_Cameroon" title="Ministry of Justice of Cameroon">Ministry of Justice</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-State_Dept_35-1"><a href="#cite_note-State_Dept-35">[35]</a></sup> The president appoints judges at all levels.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-msu_34-2"><a href="#cite_note-msu-34">[34]</a></sup> The judiciary is officially divided into tribunals, the <a href="/wiki/Court_of_Appeal_of_Cameroon" title="Court of Appeal of Cameroon">court of appeal</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_Cameroon" title="Supreme Court of Cameroon">supreme court</a>. The National Assembly elects the members of a nine-member <a href="/wiki/High_Court_of_Justice_(Cameroon)" title="High Court of Justice (Cameroon)">High Court of Justice</a> that judges high-ranking members of government in the event they are charged with high treason or harming national security.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Political_culture">Political culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cameroon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Political culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Cameroon is viewed as rife with corruption at all levels of government. In 1997, Cameroon established anti-corruption bureaus in 29 ministries, but only 25% became operational,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IRIN_39-0"><a href="#cite_note-IRIN-39">[39]</a></sup> and in 2012, <a href="/wiki/Transparency_International" title="Transparency International">Transparency International</a> placed Cameroon at number 144 on a list of 176 countries ranked from least to most corrupt.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Corruption_40-0"><a href="#cite_note-Corruption-40">[40]</a></sup> On 18 January 2006, Biya initiated an anti-corruption drive under the direction of the <a href="/wiki/National_Anti-Corruption_Observatory" title="National Anti-Corruption Observatory">National Anti-Corruption Observatory</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IRIN_39-1"><a href="#cite_note-IRIN-39">[39]</a></sup> There are several high corruption risk areas in Cameroon, for instance, customs, public health sector and public procurement.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup> Unfortunately, the corruption has gotten worse, regardless of the existing anti-corruption bureaus, as Transparency International ranked Cameroon 153 on a list of 180 countries in 2017.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Statue_d%27un_chef_coutumier_%C3%A0_Bana.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2048" data-file-width="1536" height="227" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/Statue_d%27un_chef_coutumier_%C3%A0_Bana.jpg/170px-Statue_d%27un_chef_coutumier_%C3%A0_Bana.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/Statue_d%27un_chef_coutumier_%C3%A0_Bana.jpg/255px-Statue_d%27un_chef_coutumier_%C3%A0_Bana.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/Statue_d%27un_chef_coutumier_%C3%A0_Bana.jpg/340px-Statue_d%27un_chef_coutumier_%C3%A0_Bana.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Statue_d%27un_chef_coutumier_%C3%A0_Bana.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A statue of a chief in <a href="/wiki/Bana,_Cameroon" title="Bana, Cameroon">Bana</a>, West Region.</div></div></div>
<p>Human rights organisations accuse police and military forces of mistreating and even torturing criminal suspects, ethnic minorities, <a href="/wiki/LGBT_rights_in_Cameroon" title="LGBT rights in Cameroon">homosexuals</a>, and political activists.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Amnesty_43-0"><a href="#cite_note-Amnesty-43">[43]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Freedom_House_44-0"><a href="#cite_note-Freedom_House-44">[44]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Human_Rights_Report_45-0"><a href="#cite_note-Human_Rights_Report-45">[45]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EHRC_46-0"><a href="#cite_note-EHRC-46">[46]</a></sup> Prisons are overcrowded with little access to adequate food and medical facilities,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Human_Rights_Report_45-1"><a href="#cite_note-Human_Rights_Report-45">[45]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EHRC_46-1"><a href="#cite_note-EHRC-46">[46]</a></sup> and prisons run by traditional rulers in the north are charged with holding political opponents at the behest of the government.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Freedom_House_44-1"><a href="#cite_note-Freedom_House-44">[44]</a></sup> However, since the first decade of the 21st century, an increasing number of police and gendarmes have been prosecuted for improper conduct.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Human_Rights_Report_45-2"><a href="#cite_note-Human_Rights_Report-45">[45]</a></sup> A video showing Cameroonian soldiers <a href="/wiki/Murder" title="Murder">executing</a> blindfolded women and children has emerged in 2018.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup>
</p><p>President Biya's <a href="/wiki/Cameroon_People%27s_Democratic_Movement" title="Cameroon People's Democratic Movement">Cameroon People's Democratic Movement</a> (CPDM) was the only legal political party until December 1990. Numerous regional political groups have since formed. The primary opposition is the <a href="/wiki/Social_Democratic_Front_(Cameroon)" title="Social Democratic Front (Cameroon)">Social Democratic Front</a> (SDF), based largely in the Anglophone region of the country and headed by <a href="/wiki/John_Fru_Ndi" title="John Fru Ndi">John Fru Ndi</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lergai_48-0"><a href="#cite_note-lergai-48">[48]</a></sup>
</p><p>Biya and his party have maintained control of the presidency and the National Assembly in national elections, which rivals contend were unfair.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DeLancey_9_25-1"><a href="#cite_note-DeLancey_9-25">[25]</a></sup> Human rights organisations allege that the government suppresses the freedoms of opposition groups by preventing demonstrations, disrupting meetings, and arresting opposition leaders and journalists.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Amnesty_43-1"><a href="#cite_note-Amnesty-43">[43]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Freedom_House_44-2"><a href="#cite_note-Freedom_House-44">[44]</a></sup> In particular, English-speaking people are discriminated against; protests often escalate into violent clashes and killings.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup> In 2017, President Biya shut down the Internet in the English-speaking region for 94 days, at the cost of hampering five million people, including <a href="/wiki/Silicon_Mountain" title="Silicon Mountain">Silicon Mountain</a> startups.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Freedom_House" title="Freedom House">Freedom House</a> ranks Cameroon as "not free" in terms of political rights and civil liberties.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup> The last <a href="/wiki/Cameroonian_parliamentary_election,_2013" title="Cameroonian parliamentary election, 2013">parliamentary elections</a> were held on 30 September 2013.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kandemeh_52-0"><a href="#cite_note-Kandemeh-52">[52]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_relations">Foreign relations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cameroon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Foreign relations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_Cameroon" title="Foreign relations of Cameroon">Foreign relations of Cameroon</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Paul_Biya_with_Obamas_2014.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2640" data-file-width="3960" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Paul_Biya_with_Obamas_2014.jpg/220px-Paul_Biya_with_Obamas_2014.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Paul_Biya_with_Obamas_2014.jpg/330px-Paul_Biya_with_Obamas_2014.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Paul_Biya_with_Obamas_2014.jpg/440px-Paul_Biya_with_Obamas_2014.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Paul_Biya_with_Obamas_2014.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>President <a href="/wiki/Paul_Biya" title="Paul Biya">Paul Biya</a> with U.S. President <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">Barack Obama</a> in 2014</div></div></div>
<p>Cameroon is a member of both the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Nations" title="Commonwealth of Nations">Commonwealth of Nations</a> and <a href="/wiki/Francophonie" title="Francophonie">La Francophonie</a>. 
</p><p>Its <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_Cameroon" title="Foreign relations of Cameroon">foreign policy</a> closely follows that of its main ally, France (one of its former colonial rulers).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup> Cameroon relies heavily on France for its defence,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-State_Dept_35-2"><a href="#cite_note-State_Dept-35">[35]</a></sup> although military spending is high in comparison to other sectors of government.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup>
</p><p>President Biya has engaged in a decades-long clash with the government of Nigeria over possession of the oil rich <a href="/wiki/Bakassi" title="Bakassi">Bakassi</a> peninsula.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lergai_48-1"><a href="#cite_note-lergai-48">[48]</a></sup> Cameroon and Nigeria share a 1,000 mile border and have disputed the sovereignty of the Bakassi peninsula. In 1994 Cameroon petitioned the <a href="/wiki/International_Court_of_Justice" title="International Court of Justice">International Court of Justice</a> to resolve the dispute. The two countries attempted to establish a cease-fire in 1996, however, fighting continued for years. In 2002, the ICJ ruled that the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Anglo-German_Agreement_of_1913&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Anglo-German Agreement of 1913 (page does not exist)">Anglo-German Agreement of 1913</a> gave sovereignty to Cameroon. The ruling called for a withdrawal by both countries and denied the request by Cameroon for compensation due to Nigeria's long-term occupation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup> By 2004, Nigeria had failed to meet the deadline to handover the peninsula. A UN-mediated summit in June 2006 facilitated an agreement for Nigeria to withdraw from the region and both leaders signed the Greentree Agreement.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup> The withdrawal and handover of control was completed by August 2006.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Administrative_divisions">Administrative divisions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cameroon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Administrative divisions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Regions_of_Cameroon" title="Regions of Cameroon">Regions of Cameroon</a> and <a href="/wiki/Departments_of_Cameroon" title="Departments of Cameroon">Departments of Cameroon</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Provinces_of_Cameroon_EN.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="769" data-file-width="586" height="223" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/Provinces_of_Cameroon_EN.svg/170px-Provinces_of_Cameroon_EN.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/Provinces_of_Cameroon_EN.svg/255px-Provinces_of_Cameroon_EN.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/Provinces_of_Cameroon_EN.svg/340px-Provinces_of_Cameroon_EN.svg.png 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Provinces_of_Cameroon_EN.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Cameroon is divided into 10 regions.</div></div></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Cameroon" title="Constitution of Cameroon">constitution</a> divides Cameroon into 10 semi-autonomous regions, each under the administration of an elected <a href="/wiki/Regional_Council_(Cameroon)" title="Regional Council (Cameroon)">Regional Council</a>. Each region is headed by a presidentially appointed governor.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Neba_250_33-1"><a href="#cite_note-Neba_250-33">[33]</a></sup>
</p><p>These leaders are charged with implementing the will of the president, reporting on the general mood and conditions of the regions, administering the civil service, keeping the peace, and overseeing the heads of the smaller administrative units. Governors have broad powers: they may order propaganda in their area and call in the army, <a href="/wiki/Gendarmerie" title="Gendarmerie">gendarmes</a>, and police.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Neba_250_33-2"><a href="#cite_note-Neba_250-33">[33]</a></sup> All local government officials are employees of the central government's Ministry of Territorial Administration, from which local governments also get most of their budgets.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-history_9-2"><a href="#cite_note-history-9">[9]</a></sup>
</p><p>The regions are subdivided into 58 divisions (French <i lang="fr" title="French language text">départements</i>). These are headed by presidentially appointed divisional officers (<i lang="fr" title="French language text"><a href="/wiki/Prefect" title="Prefect">préfets</a></i>). The divisions are further split into sub-divisions (<i lang="fr" title="French language text">arrondissements</i>), headed by assistant divisional officers (<i lang="fr" title="French language text">sous-prefets</i>). The districts, administered by district heads (<i lang="fr" title="French language text">chefs de district</i>), are the smallest administrative units.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-unhchr_59-0"><a href="#cite_note-unhchr-59">[59]</a></sup>
</p><p>The three northernmost regions are the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Far_North_Region_(Cameroon)" title="Far North Region (Cameroon)">Far North</a> (<i lang="fr" title="French language text">Extrême Nord</i>), <a href="/wiki/North_Region_(Cameroon)" title="North Region (Cameroon)">North</a> (<i lang="fr" title="French language text">Nord</i>), and <a href="/wiki/Adamawa_Region" title="Adamawa Region">Adamawa</a> (<i lang="fr" title="French language text">Adamaoua</i>). Directly south of them are the <a href="/wiki/Centre_Region_(Cameroon)" title="Centre Region (Cameroon)">Centre</a> (<i lang="fr" title="French language text">Centre</i>) and <a href="/wiki/East_Region_(Cameroon)" title="East Region (Cameroon)">East</a> (<i lang="fr" title="French language text">Est</i>). The <a href="/wiki/South_Region_(Cameroon)" title="South Region (Cameroon)">South Province</a> (<i lang="fr" title="French language text">Sud</i>) lies on the Gulf of Guinea and the southern border. Cameroon's western region is split into four smaller regions: the <a href="/wiki/Littoral_Region_(Cameroon)" title="Littoral Region (Cameroon)">Littoral</a> (<i lang="fr" title="French language text">Littoral</i>) and <a href="/wiki/Southwest_Region_(Cameroon)" title="Southwest Region (Cameroon)">Southwest</a> (<i lang="fr" title="French language text">Sud-Ouest</i>) regions are on the coast, and the <a href="/wiki/Northwest_Region_(Cameroon)" title="Northwest Region (Cameroon)">Northwest</a> (<i lang="fr" title="French language text">Nord-Ouest</i>) and <a href="/wiki/West_Region_(Cameroon)" title="West Region (Cameroon)">West</a> (<i lang="fr" title="French language text">Ouest</i>) regions are in the western grassfields.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-unhchr_59-1"><a href="#cite_note-unhchr-59">[59]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education_and_health">Education and health</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cameroon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Education and health">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Education_in_Cameroon" title="Education in Cameroon">Education in Cameroon</a> and <a href="/wiki/Health_in_Cameroon" title="Health in Cameroon">Health in Cameroon</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Cameroonian_school_children_gather_around_U.S._Army_Master_Sgt._John_Reid,_center,_for_a_group_photo_near_Douala,_Cameroon,_March_19,_2014,_during_Central_Accord_14_140319-A-PP104-039.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3744" data-file-width="5616" height="200" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Cameroonian_school_children_gather_around_U.S._Army_Master_Sgt._John_Reid%2C_center%2C_for_a_group_photo_near_Douala%2C_Cameroon%2C_March_19%2C_2014%2C_during_Central_Accord_14_140319-A-PP104-039.jpg/300px-thumbnail.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Cameroonian_school_children_gather_around_U.S._Army_Master_Sgt._John_Reid%2C_center%2C_for_a_group_photo_near_Douala%2C_Cameroon%2C_March_19%2C_2014%2C_during_Central_Accord_14_140319-A-PP104-039.jpg/450px-thumbnail.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Cameroonian_school_children_gather_around_U.S._Army_Master_Sgt._John_Reid%2C_center%2C_for_a_group_photo_near_Douala%2C_Cameroon%2C_March_19%2C_2014%2C_during_Central_Accord_14_140319-A-PP104-039.jpg/600px-thumbnail.jpg 2x" width="300"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Cameroonian_school_children_gather_around_U.S._Army_Master_Sgt._John_Reid,_center,_for_a_group_photo_near_Douala,_Cameroon,_March_19,_2014,_during_Central_Accord_14_140319-A-PP104-039.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>School children in Cameroon.</div></div></div>
<p>In 2013, the total adult <a href="/wiki/Literacy" title="Literacy">literacy</a> rate of Cameroon was estimated to be 71.3%. Among youths age 15-24 the literacy rate was 85.4% for males and 76.4% for females.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_60-0"><a href="#cite_note-:0-60">[60]</a></sup> Most children have access to state-run schools that are cheaper than private and religious facilities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mbaku_15_61-0"><a href="#cite_note-Mbaku_15-61">[61]</a></sup> The educational system is a mixture of British and French precedents<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup> with most instruction in English or French.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup>
</p><p>Cameroon has one of the highest school attendance rates in Africa.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mbaku_15_61-1"><a href="#cite_note-Mbaku_15-61">[61]</a></sup> Girls attend school less regularly than boys do because of cultural attitudes, domestic duties, early marriage, pregnancy, and sexual harassment. Although attendance rates are higher in the south,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mbaku_15_61-2"><a href="#cite_note-Mbaku_15-61">[61]</a></sup> a disproportionate number of teachers are stationed there, leaving northern schools chronically understaffed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Human_Rights_Report_45-3"><a href="#cite_note-Human_Rights_Report-45">[45]</a></sup> In 2013, the primary school enrollment rate was 93.5%.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_60-1"><a href="#cite_note-:0-60">[60]</a></sup>
</p><p>School attendance in Cameroon is also affected by <a href="/wiki/Child_labour" title="Child labour">child labour</a>. Indeed, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._Department_of_Labor" title="U.S. Department of Labor">U.S. Department of Labor</a> Findings on the Worst Forms of Child Labor reported that 56% of children aged 5 to 14 were working children and that almost 53% of children aged 7 to 14 combined work and school.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup> In December 2014, a <i><a href="/wiki/List_of_Goods_Produced_by_Child_Labor_or_Forced_Labor" title="List of Goods Produced by Child Labor or Forced Labor">List of Goods Produced by Child Labor or Forced Labor</a></i> issued by the <a href="/wiki/Bureau_of_International_Labor_Affairs" title="Bureau of International Labor Affairs">Bureau of International Labor Affairs</a> mentioned Cameroon among the countries that resorted to child labor in the production of cocoa.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup>
</p><p>The quality of health care is generally low.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-yqheor_66-0"><a href="#cite_note-yqheor-66">[66]</a></sup> Life expectancy at birth is estimated to be 56 years in 2012, with 48 healthy life years expected.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:1_67-0"><a href="#cite_note-:1-67">[67]</a></sup> Fertility rate remain high in Cameroon with an average of 4.8 births per woman and an average mothers' age of 19.7 years old at first birth.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:1_67-1"><a href="#cite_note-:1-67">[67]</a></sup> In Cameroon, there is only one doctor for every 5,000 people, according to the World Health Organization.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup> In 2014, just 4.1% of total GDP expenditure was allocated to healthcare.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup> Due to financial cuts in the health care system, there are few professionals. Doctors and nurses who were trained in Cameroon, emigrate because in Cameroon the payment is poor while the workload is high. Nurses are unemployed even though their help is needed. Some of them help out voluntarily so they will not lose their skills.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup> Outside the major cities, facilities are often dirty and poorly equipped.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-West_64_71-0"><a href="#cite_note-West_64-71">[71]</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2012, the top three deadly diseases were <a href="/wiki/HIV/AIDS" title="HIV/AIDS">HIV/AIDS</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lower_respiratory_infection" title="Lower respiratory infection">Lower Respiratory Infection</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Diarrheal_diseases" title="Diarrheal diseases">Diarrheal Diseases</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:1_67-2"><a href="#cite_note-:1-67">[67]</a></sup> Endemic diseases include <a href="/wiki/Dengue_fever" title="Dengue fever">dengue fever</a>, <a href="/wiki/Filariasis" title="Filariasis">filariasis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Leishmaniasis" title="Leishmaniasis">leishmaniasis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Malaria" title="Malaria">malaria</a>, <a href="/wiki/Meningitis" title="Meningitis">meningitis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Schistosomiasis" title="Schistosomiasis">schistosomiasis</a>, and <a href="/wiki/African_trypanosomiasis" title="African trypanosomiasis">sleeping sickness</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/HIV" title="HIV">HIV</a>/<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/AIDS" title="AIDS">AIDS</a> prevalence rate in 2016 was estimated at 3.8% for those aged 15–49,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:2_73-0"><a href="#cite_note-:2-73">[73]</a></sup> although a strong stigma against the illness keeps the number of reported cases artificially low.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-yqheor_66-1"><a href="#cite_note-yqheor-66">[66]</a></sup> 46,000 children under age 14 were estimated to be living with HIV in 2016. In Cameroon, 58% of those living with HIV know their status, and just 37% receive <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Antiretroviral" title="Antiretroviral">ARV</a> treatment. In 2016, 29,000 death due to AIDS occurred in both adults and children.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:2_73-1"><a href="#cite_note-:2-73">[73]</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Breast_ironing" title="Breast ironing">Breast ironing</a>, a traditional practice that is prevalent in Cameroon, may affect girls' health.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Female_genital_mutilation" title="Female genital mutilation">Female genital mutilation</a> (FGM), while not widespread, is practiced among some populations; according to a 2013 UNICEF report,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UNICEF2013p27_78-0"><a href="#cite_note-UNICEF2013p27-78">[78]</a></sup> 1% of women in Cameroon have undergone FGM. Also impacting women and girls' health, the contraceptive prevalence rate is estimated to be just 34.4% in 2014. <a href="/wiki/Traditional_medicine" title="Traditional medicine">Traditional healers</a> remain a popular alternative to <a href="/wiki/Evidence-based_medicine" title="Evidence-based medicine">evidence-based medicine</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lantum_79-0"><a href="#cite_note-Lantum-79">[79]</a></sup>
</p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cameroon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Cameroon" title="Geography of Cameroon">Geography of Cameroon</a> and <a href="/wiki/Geology_of_Cameroon" title="Geology of Cameroon">Geology of Cameroon</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Cameroon_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1900" data-file-width="1900" height="300" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/Cameroon_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg/300px-Cameroon_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/Cameroon_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg/450px-Cameroon_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/Cameroon_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg/600px-Cameroon_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg.png 2x" width="300"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Cameroon_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Cameroon map of Köppen climate classification.</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Rhumsiki_Peak.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="750" data-file-width="1000" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/Rhumsiki_Peak.jpg/220px-Rhumsiki_Peak.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/Rhumsiki_Peak.jpg/330px-Rhumsiki_Peak.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/Rhumsiki_Peak.jpg/440px-Rhumsiki_Peak.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Rhumsiki_Peak.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Volcanic_plugs" title="Volcanic plugs">Volcanic plugs</a> dot the landscape near <a href="/wiki/Rhumsiki" title="Rhumsiki">Rhumsiki</a>, Far North Region.</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Dja_Faunal_Reserve-109438.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1944" data-file-width="2592" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Dja_Faunal_Reserve-109438.jpg/220px-Dja_Faunal_Reserve-109438.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Dja_Faunal_Reserve-109438.jpg/330px-Dja_Faunal_Reserve-109438.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Dja_Faunal_Reserve-109438.jpg/440px-Dja_Faunal_Reserve-109438.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Dja_Faunal_Reserve-109438.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Dja_Faunal_Reserve" title="Dja Faunal Reserve">Dja Faunal Reserve</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>At 475,442 square kilometres (183,569 sq mi), Cameroon is the world's 53rd-largest country.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Demographic_Yearbook_80-0"><a href="#cite_note-Demographic_Yearbook-80">[80]</a></sup> It is slightly larger than the nation of <a href="/wiki/Sweden" title="Sweden">Sweden</a> and the state of California; Cameroon is comparable in size to <a href="/wiki/Papua_New_Guinea" title="Papua New Guinea">Papua New Guinea</a>. The country is located in <a href="/wiki/Central_Africa" title="Central Africa">Central</a> and West Africa, known as the hinge of Africa, on the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bight_of_Bonny" title="Bight of Bonny">Bight of Bonny</a>, part of the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Guinea" title="Gulf of Guinea">Gulf of Guinea</a> and the Atlantic Ocean.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup> Cameroon lies between latitudes <a href="/wiki/1st_parallel_north" title="1st parallel north">1°</a> and <a href="/wiki/13th_parallel_north" title="13th parallel north">13°N</a>, and longitudes <a href="/wiki/8th_meridian_east" title="8th meridian east">8°</a> and <a href="/wiki/17th_meridian_east" title="17th meridian east">17°E</a>. Cameroon controls 12 nautical miles of the Atlantic Ocean.
</p><p>Tourist literature describes Cameroon as "Africa in miniature" because it exhibits all major climates and vegetation of the continent: coast, desert, mountains, rainforest, and savanna.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup> The country's neighbours are Nigeria and the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Ocean" title="Atlantic Ocean">Atlantic Ocean</a> to the west; <a href="/wiki/Chad" title="Chad">Chad</a> to the northeast; the <a href="/wiki/Central_African_Republic" title="Central African Republic">Central African Republic</a> to the east; and <a href="/wiki/Equatorial_Guinea" title="Equatorial Guinea">Equatorial Guinea</a>, Gabon and the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Republic of the Congo">Republic of the Congo</a> to the south.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CIA_1-6"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-1">[1]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Elephants_around_tree_in_Waza,_Cameroon.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1036" data-file-width="1384" height="225" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Elephants_around_tree_in_Waza%2C_Cameroon.jpg/300px-Elephants_around_tree_in_Waza%2C_Cameroon.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Elephants_around_tree_in_Waza%2C_Cameroon.jpg/450px-Elephants_around_tree_in_Waza%2C_Cameroon.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Elephants_around_tree_in_Waza%2C_Cameroon.jpg/600px-Elephants_around_tree_in_Waza%2C_Cameroon.jpg 2x" width="300"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Elephants_around_tree_in_Waza,_Cameroon.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Elephants in <a href="/wiki/Waza_National_Park" title="Waza National Park">Waza National Park</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>Cameroon is divided into five major geographic zones distinguished by dominant physical, climatic, and vegetative features. The coastal plain extends 15 to 150 kilometres (9 to 93 mi) inland from the Gulf of Guinea<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Fomensky_83-0"><a href="#cite_note-Fomensky-83">[83]</a></sup> and has an average elevation of 90 metres (295 ft).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup> Exceedingly hot and humid with a short <a href="/wiki/Dry_season" title="Dry season">dry season</a>, this belt is densely forested and includes some of the <a href="/wiki/Debundscha" title="Debundscha">wettest places</a> on earth, part of the <a href="/wiki/Cross-Sanaga-Bioko_coastal_forests" title="Cross-Sanaga-Bioko coastal forests">Cross-Sanaga-Bioko coastal forests</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Extremes_86-0"><a href="#cite_note-Extremes-86">[86]</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/South_Cameroon_Plateau" title="South Cameroon Plateau">South Cameroon Plateau</a> rises from the coastal plain to an average elevation of 650 metres (2,133 ft).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Neba_16_87-0"><a href="#cite_note-Neba_16-87">[87]</a></sup> Equatorial rainforest dominates this region, although its alternation between <a href="/wiki/Wet_season" title="Wet season">wet</a> and dry seasons makes it is less humid than the coast. This area is part of the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Equatorial_coastal_forests" title="Atlantic Equatorial coastal forests">Atlantic Equatorial coastal forests</a> <a href="/wiki/Ecoregion" title="Ecoregion">ecoregion</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hills_near_Ngaoundal.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="567" data-file-width="1000" height="125" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Hills_near_Ngaoundal.jpg/220px-Hills_near_Ngaoundal.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Hills_near_Ngaoundal.jpg/330px-Hills_near_Ngaoundal.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Hills_near_Ngaoundal.jpg/440px-Hills_near_Ngaoundal.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Hills_near_Ngaoundal.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Countryside near <a href="/wiki/Ngaoundal" title="Ngaoundal">Ngaoundal</a> in Cameroon's <a href="/wiki/Adamawa_Region" title="Adamawa Region">Adamawa Region</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>An irregular chain of mountains, hills, and plateaus known as the <a href="/wiki/Cameroon_line" title="Cameroon line">Cameroon range</a> extends from <a href="/wiki/Mount_Cameroon" title="Mount Cameroon">Mount Cameroon</a> on the coast—Cameroon's highest point at 4,095 metres (13,435 ft)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Neba_17_89-0"><a href="#cite_note-Neba_17-89">[89]</a></sup>—almost to <a href="/wiki/Lake_Chad" title="Lake Chad">Lake Chad</a> at Cameroon's northern border at 13°05'N. This region has a mild climate, particularly on the <a href="/wiki/Western_High_Plateau" title="Western High Plateau">Western High Plateau</a>, although rainfall is high. Its soils are among Cameroon's most fertile, especially around volcanic Mount Cameroon.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Neba_17_89-1"><a href="#cite_note-Neba_17-89">[89]</a></sup> Volcanism here has created <a href="/wiki/Crater_lake" title="Crater lake">crater lakes</a>. On 21 August 1986, one of these, <a href="/wiki/Lake_Nyos" title="Lake Nyos">Lake Nyos</a>, belched carbon dioxide and killed between 1,700 and 2,000 people.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup> This area has been delineated by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/World_Wildlife_Fund" title="World Wildlife Fund">World Wildlife Fund</a> as the <a href="/wiki/Cameroonian_Highlands_forests" title="Cameroonian Highlands forests">Cameroonian Highlands forests</a> ecoregion.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup>
</p><p>The southern plateau rises northward to the grassy, rugged <a href="/wiki/Adamawa_Plateau" title="Adamawa Plateau">Adamawa Plateau</a>. This feature stretches from the western mountain area and forms a barrier between the country's north and south. Its average elevation is 1,100 metres (3,609 ft),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Neba_16_87-1"><a href="#cite_note-Neba_16-87">[87]</a></sup> and its average temperature ranges from 22 °C (71.6 °F) to 25 °C (77 °F) with high rainfall between April and October peaking in July and August.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gwanfogbe_92-0"><a href="#cite_note-Gwanfogbe-92">[92]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup> The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/East_Sudanian_savanna" title="East Sudanian savanna">northern lowland region</a> extends from the edge of the Adamawa to Lake Chad with an average elevation of 300 to 350 metres (984 to 1,148 ft).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Neba_17_89-2"><a href="#cite_note-Neba_17-89">[89]</a></sup> Its characteristic vegetation is savanna scrub and grass. This is an arid region with sparse rainfall and high median temperatures.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Green_94-0"><a href="#cite_note-Green-94">[94]</a></sup>
</p><p>Cameroon has four patterns of drainage. In the south, the principal rivers are the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ntem_River" title="Ntem River">Ntem</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nyong_River" title="Nyong River">Nyong</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sanaga_River" title="Sanaga River">Sanaga</a>, and Wouri. These flow southwestward or westward directly into the Gulf of Guinea. The <a href="/wiki/Dja_River" title="Dja River">Dja</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kad%C3%A9%C3%AF_River" title="Kadéï River">Kadéï</a> drain southeastward into the <a href="/wiki/Congo_River" title="Congo River">Congo River</a>. In northern Cameroon, the <a href="/wiki/Benue_River" title="Benue River">Bénoué River</a> runs north and west and empties into the <a href="/wiki/Niger_River" title="Niger River">Niger</a>. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Logon_River" title="Logon River">Logone</a> flows northward into Lake Chad, which Cameroon shares with three neighbouring countries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy_and_infrastructure">Economy and infrastructure</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cameroon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Economy and infrastructure">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Cameroon" title="Economy of Cameroon">Economy of Cameroon</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Douala.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="272" data-file-width="415" height="144" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Douala.JPG/220px-Douala.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Douala.JPG/330px-Douala.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/9/99/Douala.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Douala.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Douala" title="Douala">Douala</a>, the economic capital of Cameroon</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Limbe1.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="334" data-file-width="500" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Limbe1.png/220px-Limbe1.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Limbe1.png/330px-Limbe1.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Limbe1.png/440px-Limbe1.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Limbe1.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A touristic area in <a href="/wiki/Limbe,_Cameroon" title="Limbe, Cameroon">Limbe</a></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:YaoundeSportPalace.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="375" data-file-width="500" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/YaoundeSportPalace.png/220px-YaoundeSportPalace.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/YaoundeSportPalace.png/330px-YaoundeSportPalace.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/YaoundeSportPalace.png/440px-YaoundeSportPalace.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:YaoundeSportPalace.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Yaound%C3%A9" title="Yaoundé">Yaoundé</a> Sport palace</div></div></div>
<p>Cameroon's per-capita GDP (<a href="/wiki/Purchasing_power_parity" title="Purchasing power parity">Purchasing power parity</a>) was estimated as US$2,300 in 2008,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CIA_1-7"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-1">[1]</a></sup> one of the ten highest in <a href="/wiki/Sub-Saharan_Africa" title="Sub-Saharan Africa">sub-Saharan Africa</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Musa_Biya_plan_96-0"><a href="#cite_note-Musa_Biya_plan-96">[96]</a></sup> Major <a href="/wiki/Export" title="Export">export</a> markets include France, Italy, South Korea, Spain, and the United Kingdom.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CIA_1-8"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-1">[1]</a></sup> Cameroon is aiming to become an emerging country by 2035.
</p><p>Cameroon has had a decade of strong economic performance, with GDP growing at an average of 4% per year. During the 2004–2008 period, public debt was reduced from over 60% of GDP to 10% and official reserves quadrupled to over USD 3 billion.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup> Cameroon is part of the <a href="/wiki/Bank_of_Central_African_States" title="Bank of Central African States">Bank of Central African States</a> (of which it is the dominant economy),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Musa_Biya_plan_96-1"><a href="#cite_note-Musa_Biya_plan-96">[96]</a></sup> the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Customs_and_Economic_Union_of_Central_Africa" title="Customs and Economic Union of Central Africa">Customs and Economic Union of Central Africa</a> (UDEAC) and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Organization_for_the_Harmonization_of_Business_Law_in_Africa" title="Organization for the Harmonization of Business Law in Africa">Organization for the Harmonization of Business Law in Africa</a> (OHADA).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ohada.com_98-0"><a href="#cite_note-ohada.com-98">[98]</a></sup> Its currency is the <a href="/wiki/CFA_franc" title="CFA franc">CFA franc</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CIA_1-9"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-1">[1]</a></sup>
</p><p>Unemployment was estimated at 4.4% in 2014,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup> and about a third of the population was living below the international <a href="/wiki/Poverty_threshold" title="Poverty threshold">poverty threshold</a> of US$1.25 a day in 2009.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup> Since the late 1980s, Cameroon has been following programmes advocated by the <a href="/wiki/World_Bank" title="World Bank">World Bank</a> and <a href="/wiki/International_Monetary_Fund" title="International Monetary Fund">International Monetary Fund</a> (IMF) to reduce poverty, privatise industries, and increase economic growth.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-State_Dept_35-3"><a href="#cite_note-State_Dept-35">[35]</a></sup> The government has taken measures to encourage <a href="/wiki/Tourism_in_Cameroon" title="Tourism in Cameroon">tourism</a> in the country.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup>
</p><p>Cameroon's natural resources are very well suited to agriculture and arboriculture. An estimated 70% of the population farms, and agriculture comprised an estimated 19.8% of GDP in 2009.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CIA_1-10"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-1">[1]</a></sup> Most agriculture is done at the subsistence scale by local farmers using simple tools. They sell their surplus produce, and some maintain separate fields for commercial use. Urban centres are particularly reliant on peasant agriculture for their foodstuffs. Soils and climate on the coast encourage extensive commercial cultivation of bananas, cocoa, oil palms, rubber, and tea. Inland on the South Cameroon Plateau, cash crops include coffee, sugar, and tobacco. Coffee is a major cash crop in the western highlands, and in the north, natural conditions favour crops such as cotton, groundnuts, and rice. Reliance on agricultural exports makes Cameroon vulnerable to shifts in their prices.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CIA_1-11"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-1">[1]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Fulani_herd_in_the_dust.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="610" data-file-width="1024" height="131" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/Fulani_herd_in_the_dust.jpg/220px-Fulani_herd_in_the_dust.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/Fulani_herd_in_the_dust.jpg/330px-Fulani_herd_in_the_dust.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/Fulani_herd_in_the_dust.jpg/440px-Fulani_herd_in_the_dust.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Fulani_herd_in_the_dust.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A <a href="/wiki/Fula_people" title="Fula people">Fulani</a> herder drives his cattle in northern Cameroon.</div></div></div>
<p>Livestock are raised throughout the country.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup> Fishing employs 5,000 people and provides over 100,000 tons of seafood each year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-awf_104-0"><a href="#cite_note-awf-104">[104]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Bushmeat" title="Bushmeat">Bushmeat</a>, long a staple food for rural Cameroonians, is today a delicacy in the country's urban centres. The commercial bushmeat trade has now surpassed deforestation as the main threat to wildlife in Cameroon.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup>
</p><p>The southern rainforest has vast timber reserves, estimated to cover 37% of Cameroon's total land area.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-awf_104-1"><a href="#cite_note-awf-104">[104]</a></sup> However, large areas of the forest are difficult to reach. Logging, largely handled by foreign-owned firms,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-awf_104-2"><a href="#cite_note-awf-104">[104]</a></sup> provides the government US$60 million a year in taxes (as of  1998<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Cameroon&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>), and laws mandate the safe and sustainable exploitation of timber. Nevertheless, in practice, the industry is one of the least regulated in Cameroon.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup>
</p><p>Factory-based industry accounted for an estimated 29.7% of GDP in 2009.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CIA_1-12"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-1">[1]</a></sup> More than 75% of Cameroon's industrial strength is located in <a href="/wiki/Douala" title="Douala">Douala</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bonab%C3%A9ri" title="Bonabéri">Bonabéri</a>. Cameroon possesses substantial mineral resources, but these are not extensively mined (see <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mining_in_Cameroon" title="Mining in Cameroon">Mining in Cameroon</a></i>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-State_Dept_35-4"><a href="#cite_note-State_Dept-35">[35]</a></sup> Petroleum exploitation has fallen since 1986, but this is still a substantial sector such that dips in prices have a strong effect on the economy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup> Rapids and waterfalls obstruct the southern rivers, but these sites offer opportunities for hydroelectric development and supply most of Cameroon's energy. The Sanaga River powers the largest hydroelectric station, located at Edéa. The rest of Cameroon's energy comes from oil-powered thermal engines. Much of the country remains without reliable power supplies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Transport_in_Cameroon" title="Transport in Cameroon">Transport in Cameroon</a> is often difficult. Except for the several relatively good <a href="/wiki/Toll_road" title="Toll road">toll roads</a> which connect major cities (all of them one-lane) roads are poorly maintained and subject to inclement weather, since only 10% of the roadways are tarred.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CIA_1-13"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-1">[1]</a></sup> Roadblocks often serve little other purpose than to allow police and gendarmes to collect bribes from travellers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup> Road banditry has long hampered transport along the eastern and western borders, and since 2005, the problem has intensified in the east as the <a href="/wiki/Central_African_Republic" title="Central African Republic">Central African Republic</a> has further destabilised.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Musa_Gunmen_111-0"><a href="#cite_note-Musa_Gunmen-111">[111]</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Intercity_bus_service" title="Intercity bus service">Intercity bus services</a> run by multiple private companies connect all major cities. They are the most popular means of transportation followed by the rail service <i><a href="/wiki/Camrail" title="Camrail">Camrail</a></i>. Rail service runs from <a href="/wiki/Kumba" title="Kumba">Kumba</a> in the west to <a href="/wiki/B%C3%A9labo" title="Bélabo">Bélabo</a> in the east and north to <a href="/wiki/Ngaound%C3%A9r%C3%A9" title="Ngaoundéré">Ngaoundéré</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112"><a href="#cite_note-112">[112]</a></sup> International airports are located in <a href="/wiki/Douala_International_Airport" title="Douala International Airport">Douala</a> and <a href="/wiki/Yaound%C3%A9_Nsimalen_International_Airport" title="Yaoundé Nsimalen International Airport">Yaoundé</a>, with a third under construction in <a href="/wiki/Maroua" title="Maroua">Maroua</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113"><a href="#cite_note-113">[113]</a></sup> Douala is the country's principal seaport.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114"><a href="#cite_note-114">[114]</a></sup> In the north, the Bénoué River is seasonally navigable from Garoua across into Nigeria.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115"><a href="#cite_note-115">[115]</a></sup>
</p><p>Although press freedoms have improved since the first decade of the 21st century, the press is corrupt and beholden to special interests and political groups.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Reporters_116-0"><a href="#cite_note-Reporters-116">[116]</a></sup> Newspapers routinely self-censor to avoid government reprisals.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Human_Rights_Report_45-4"><a href="#cite_note-Human_Rights_Report-45">[45]</a></sup> The major radio and television stations are state-run and other <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Communications_in_Cameroon" title="Communications in Cameroon">communications</a>, such as land-based telephones and telegraphs, are largely under government control.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117"><a href="#cite_note-117">[117]</a></sup> However, cell phone networks and Internet providers have increased dramatically since the first decade of the 21st century<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118"><a href="#cite_note-118">[118]</a></sup> and are largely unregulated.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Freedom_House_44-3"><a href="#cite_note-Freedom_House-44">[44]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Military">Military</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cameroon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Military">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Cameroonian_Armed_Forces" title="Cameroonian Armed Forces">Cameroonian Armed Forces</a></div>
<p>The Cameroon Armed Forces, (French: <i>Forces armées camerounaises</i>, FAC) as of  2015<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Cameroon&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, consists of the country's army (<a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a>: <i>Armée de Terre</i>), the country's navy (French: <i>Marine Nationale de la République</i> (MNR), includes naval infantry), the Cameroonian Air Force (French: <i>Armée de l'Air du Cameroun</i>, AAC), Fire Fighter Corps, Rapid Intervention Brigade and the <a href="/wiki/Gendarmerie" title="Gendarmerie">Gendarmerie</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AFRICA_::_CAMEROON_119-0"><a href="#cite_note-AFRICA_::_CAMEROON-119">[119]</a></sup>
</p><p>Males and females that are 18 years of age up to 23 years of age and have graduated high school are eligible for military service. Those that do so are obliged 4 years of service. There is no conscription in Cameroon, but the government makes periodic calls for volunteers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AFRICA_::_CAMEROON_119-1"><a href="#cite_note-AFRICA_::_CAMEROON-119">[119]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cameroon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Cameroon" title="Demographics of Cameroon">Demographics of Cameroon</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:442px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:YaoundePanoramicView.jpeg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="168" data-file-width="567" height="130" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/YaoundePanoramicView.jpeg/440px-YaoundePanoramicView.jpeg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/a/a3/YaoundePanoramicView.jpeg 1.5x" width="440"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:YaoundePanoramicView.jpeg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Yaound%C3%A9" title="Yaoundé">Yaoundé</a> panoramic view.</div></div></div>
<table class="wikitable" style="float: right; margin-left: 10px">
<tbody><tr>
<th colspan="4" style="text-align:center; background:#cfb;">Population in Cameroon<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IEApop2011_120-0"><a href="#cite_note-IEApop2011-120">[120]</a></sup>
</th></tr>
<tr>
<th style="background:#cfb;">Year
</th>
<th style="background:#cfb;">Million

<td style="text-align:right;">7.0

</td></tr>
