</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>The population total in Cameroon was 23,439,189 in 2016.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UN_WPP_3-1"><a href="#cite_note-UN_WPP-3">[3]</a></sup> The life expectancy is 56 years (55.9 years for males and 58.6 years for females).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CIA_1-14"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-1">[1]</a></sup>
</p><p>According to the latest census, Cameroon still has slightly more women (50.6%) than men (49.4%). Nearly 60% of the population is under age 25. People over 65 years of age account for only 3.2% of the total population.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CIA_1-15"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-1">[1]</a></sup>
</p><p>Cameroon's population is almost evenly divided between urban and rural dwellers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-West_3_121-0"><a href="#cite_note-West_3-121">[121]</a></sup> Population density is highest in the large urban centres, the western highlands, and the northeastern plain.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122"><a href="#cite_note-122">[122]</a></sup> Douala, Yaoundé, and <a href="/wiki/Garoua" title="Garoua">Garoua</a> are the largest cities. In contrast, the Adamawa Plateau, southeastern Bénoué depression, and most of the South Cameroon Plateau are sparsely populated.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123"><a href="#cite_note-123">[123]</a></sup>
</p><p>According to the <a href="/wiki/World_Health_Organization" title="World Health Organization">World Health Organization</a>, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fertility_rate" title="Fertility rate">fertility rate</a> was 4.8 in 2013 with a population growth rate of 2.56%.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:1_67-3"><a href="#cite_note-:1-67">[67]</a></sup>
</p><p>People from the overpopulated western highlands and the underdeveloped north are moving to the coastal plantation zone and urban centres for employment.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-124"><a href="#cite_note-124">[124]</a></sup> Smaller movements are occurring as workers seek employment in lumber mills and plantations in the south and east.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125"><a href="#cite_note-125">[125]</a></sup> Although the national sex ratio is relatively even, these out-migrants are primarily males, which leads to unbalanced ratios in some regions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-126"><a href="#cite_note-126">[126]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Maison_obus.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="688" data-file-width="1060" height="195" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/Maison_obus.jpg/300px-Maison_obus.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/Maison_obus.jpg/450px-Maison_obus.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/Maison_obus.jpg/600px-Maison_obus.jpg 2x" width="300"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Maison_obus.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The homes of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Musgum_dwelling_units" title="Musgum dwelling units">Musgum</a>, in the Far North Region, are made of earth and grass.</div></div></div>
<p>Both <a href="/wiki/Monogamy" title="Monogamy">monogamous</a> and <a href="/wiki/Polygamy" title="Polygamy">polygamous</a> marriage are practised, and the average Cameroonian family is large and extended.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-127"><a href="#cite_note-127">[127]</a></sup> In the north, women tend to the home, and men herd cattle or work as farmers. In the south, women grow the family's food, and men provide meat and grow cash crops. Like most societies, Cameroonian society is male-dominated, and violence and discrimination against women is common.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Freedom_House_44-4"><a href="#cite_note-Freedom_House-44">[44]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Human_Rights_Report_45-5"><a href="#cite_note-Human_Rights_Report-45">[45]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-128"><a href="#cite_note-128">[128]</a></sup>
</p><p>Estimates identify anywhere from 230 to 282 different folks and linguistic groups in Cameroon.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-129"><a href="#cite_note-129">[129]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-130"><a href="#cite_note-130">[130]</a></sup> The Adamawa Plateau broadly bisects these into northern and southern divisions. The northern peoples are Sudanese groups, who live in the central highlands and the northern lowlands, and the Fulani, who are spread throughout northern Cameroon. A small number of <a href="/wiki/Baggara" title="Baggara">Shuwa</a> Arabs live near Lake Chad. Southern Cameroon is inhabited by speakers of <a href="/wiki/Bantu_languages" title="Bantu languages">Bantu</a> and <a href="/wiki/Semi-Bantu" title="Semi-Bantu">Semi-Bantu</a> languages. Bantu-speaking groups inhabit the coastal and equatorial zones, while speakers of Semi-Bantu languages live in the Western grassfields. Some 5,000 Gyele and Baka <a href="/wiki/Pygmy_peoples" title="Pygmy peoples">Pygmy peoples</a> roam the southeastern and coastal rainforests or live in small, roadside settlements.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-131"><a href="#cite_note-131">[131]</a></sup> Nigerians make up the largest group of foreign nationals.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-132"><a href="#cite_note-132">[132]</a></sup>
</p><p><br/>
</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Refugees">Refugees</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cameroon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Refugees">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Refugees_in_Cameroon" title="Refugees in Cameroon">Refugees in Cameroon</a></div>
<p>In 2007, Cameroon hosted a total population of refugees and asylum seekers of approximately 97,400. Of these, 49,300 were from the Central African Republic (many driven west by war),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RCross_133-0"><a href="#cite_note-RCross-133">[133]</a></sup> 41,600 from <a href="/wiki/Chad" title="Chad">Chad</a>, and 2,900 from <a href="/wiki/Nigeria" title="Nigeria">Nigeria</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-World_Refugee_Survey_2008_134-0"><a href="#cite_note-World_Refugee_Survey_2008-134">[134]</a></sup> Kidnappings of Cameroonian citizens by Central African bandits have increased since 2005.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Musa_Gunmen_111-1"><a href="#cite_note-Musa_Gunmen-111">[111]</a></sup>
</p><p>In the first months of 2014, thousands of refugees fleeing the violence in the <a href="/wiki/Central_African_Republic" title="Central African Republic">Central African Republic</a> arrived in Cameroon.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-135"><a href="#cite_note-135">[135]</a></sup>
</p><p>On 4 June 2014, AlertNet reported:
</p>
<blockquote>
<p>Almost 90,000 people have fled to neighbouring Cameroon since December and up to 2,000 a week, mostly women and children, are still crossing the border, the United Nations said.
</p><p>"Women and children are arriving in Cameroon in a shocking state, after weeks, sometimes months, on the road, foraging for food," said Ertharin Cousin, executive director of the <a href="/wiki/World_Food_Programme" title="World Food Programme">World Food Programme</a> (WFP).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-136"><a href="#cite_note-136">[136]</a></sup>
</p>
</blockquote>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Languages">Languages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cameroon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Languages">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_Cameroon" title="Languages of Cameroon">Languages of Cameroon</a></div>
<p>Both English and French are official languages, although French is by far the most understood language (more than 80%).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-137"><a href="#cite_note-137">[137]</a></sup> German, the language of the original colonisers, has long since been displaced by French and English. <a href="/wiki/Cameroonian_Pidgin_English" title="Cameroonian Pidgin English">Cameroonian Pidgin English</a> is the lingua franca in the formerly British-administered territories.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-138"><a href="#cite_note-138">[138]</a></sup> A mixture of English, French, and Pidgin called <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Frananglais" title="Frananglais">Frananglais</a> has been gaining popularity in urban centres since the mid-1970s.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-139"><a href="#cite_note-139">[139]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Niba_140-0"><a href="#cite_note-Niba-140">[140]</a></sup> The government encourages bilingualism in English and French, and as such, official government documents, new legislation, ballots, among others, are written and provided in both languages. As part of the initiative to encourage bilingualism in Cameroon, six of the eight universities in the country are entirely bilingual.
</p><p>In addition to the colonial languages, there are approximately 250 other languages spoken by nearly 20 million Cameroonians.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-141"><a href="#cite_note-141">[141]</a></sup> It is because of this that Cameroon is considered one of the most linguistically diverse countries in the world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-142"><a href="#cite_note-142">[142]</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2017 there were language protests by the anglophone population against perceived oppression by the francophone. The military was deployed against the protesters and people have been killed, hundreds imprisoned and thousands fled the country.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-143"><a href="#cite_note-143">[143]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cameroon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_Cameroon" title="Religion in Cameroon">Religion in Cameroon</a></div>

<td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; text-align: right;">3%</td>
</tr>
</tbody></table>
</div>
</div>
<p>Cameroon has a high level of <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_Cameroon" title="Religion in Cameroon">religious freedom</a> and diversity.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Human_Rights_Report_45-6"><a href="#cite_note-Human_Rights_Report-45">[45]</a></sup> The predominant faith is <a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">Christianity</a>, practised by about two-thirds of the population, while <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Islam</a> is a significant minority faith, adhered to by about one-fifth. In addition, traditional faiths are practised by many. Muslims are most concentrated in the north, while Christians are concentrated primarily in the southern and western regions, but practitioners of both faiths can be found throughout the country.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IRFR_145-1"><a href="#cite_note-IRFR-145">[145]</a></sup> Large cities have significant populations of both groups.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IRFR_145-2"><a href="#cite_note-IRFR-145">[145]</a></sup> Muslims in Cameroon are divided into <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sufis" title="Sufis">Sufis</a> (and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Salafi" title="Salafi">Salafis</a>),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-The_Economist_146-0"><a href="#cite_note-The_Economist-146">[146]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Shia" title="Shia">Shias</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Non-denominational_Muslims" title="Non-denominational Muslims">non-denominational Muslims</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-The_Economist_146-1"><a href="#cite_note-The_Economist-146">[146]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-147"><a href="#cite_note-147">[147]</a></sup>
</p><p>People from the North-West and South-West provinces, which used to be a part of <a href="/wiki/British_Cameroons" title="British Cameroons">British Cameroons</a>, have the highest proportion of Protestants. The French-speaking regions of the southern and western regions are largely Catholic.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IRFR_145-3"><a href="#cite_note-IRFR-145">[145]</a></sup> Southern ethnic groups predominantly follow Christian or traditional African <a href="/wiki/Animism" title="Animism">animist</a> beliefs, or a <a href="/wiki/Syncretism" title="Syncretism">syncretic</a> combination of the two. People widely believe in witchcraft, and the government outlaws such practices.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Geschiere_148-0"><a href="#cite_note-Geschiere-148">[148]</a></sup> Suspected witches are often subject to mob violence.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Human_Rights_Report_45-7"><a href="#cite_note-Human_Rights_Report-45">[45]</a></sup> The Islamist jihadist group Ansar al Islam has been reported as operating in North Cameroon.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-149"><a href="#cite_note-149">[149]</a></sup>
</p><p>In the northern regions, the locally dominant Fulani ethnic group is mostly Muslim, but the overall population is fairly evenly divided among Muslims, Christians, and followers of indigenous religious beliefs (called <i><a href="/wiki/Kirdi" title="Kirdi">Kirdi</a></i> ("pagan") by the Fulani).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IRFR_145-4"><a href="#cite_note-IRFR-145">[145]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Bamum_people" title="Bamum people">Bamum</a> ethnic group of the West Region is largely Muslim.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IRFR_145-5"><a href="#cite_note-IRFR-145">[145]</a></sup> Native traditional religions are practised in rural areas throughout the country but rarely are practised publicly in cities, in part because many indigenous religious groups are intrinsically local in character.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IRFR_145-6"><a href="#cite_note-IRFR-145">[145]</a></sup>
</p><p>The Norwegian Missionary Society first established a mission in Cameroon in the early 1920s. Many of the churches still stands. At the time there were few Christians but now there are many. In cooperation with the local Evangelical Lutheran Church of Cameroon EELC and the American ELCA the NMS built several hospitals among these the Protestant Hospital of Ngaoundéré, high schools and several other institutions. Ngaoundéré once held one of the largest Norwegian contingencies of any place in the world, with over 100 Norwegians living there in the 1980s. Some of the families have been there in several generations among these Kaldhol, Bjaanes, Stavenjord and Dankel. The neighbourhood was even dubbed "Norvège" ("Norway" in French).
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cameroon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Cameroon" title="Culture of Cameroon">Culture of Cameroon</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Media">Media</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cameroon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Media">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Media_of_Cameroon" title="Media of Cameroon">Media of Cameroon</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Music_and_dance">Music and dance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cameroon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Music and dance">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Cameroon" title="Music of Cameroon">Music of Cameroon</a> and <a href="/wiki/Public_holidays_in_Cameroon" title="Public holidays in Cameroon">Public holidays in Cameroon</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Baka_dancers_June_2006.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="336" data-file-width="313" height="236" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Baka_dancers_June_2006.jpg/220px-Baka_dancers_June_2006.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/5/54/Baka_dancers_June_2006.jpg 1.5x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Baka_dancers_June_2006.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Dancers greet visitors to the East Region.</div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Music_of_Cameroon" title="Music of Cameroon">Music</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dance_in_Cameroon" title="Dance in Cameroon">dance</a> are an integral part of Cameroonian ceremonies, festivals, social gatherings, and storytelling.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-150"><a href="#cite_note-150">[150]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-West_18_151-0"><a href="#cite_note-West_18-151">[151]</a></sup> Traditional dances are highly choreographed and separate men and women or forbid participation by one sex altogether.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-152"><a href="#cite_note-152">[152]</a></sup> The goals of dances range from pure entertainment to religious devotion.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-West_18_151-1"><a href="#cite_note-West_18-151">[151]</a></sup> Traditionally, music is transmitted orally. In a typical performance, a chorus of singers echoes a soloist.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mbaku_189_153-0"><a href="#cite_note-Mbaku_189-153">[153]</a></sup>
</p><p>Musical accompaniment may be as simple as clapping hands and stomping feet,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-154"><a href="#cite_note-154">[154]</a></sup> but traditional instruments include bells worn by dancers, clappers, drums and <a href="/wiki/Talking_drum" title="Talking drum">talking drums</a>, flutes, horns, rattles, scrapers, stringed instruments, whistles, and xylophones; the exact combination varies with ethnic group and region. Some performers sing complete songs by themselves, accompanied by a harplike instrument.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mbaku_189_153-1"><a href="#cite_note-Mbaku_189-153">[153]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-155"><a href="#cite_note-155">[155]</a></sup>
</p><p>Popular music styles include <a href="/wiki/Ambasse_bey" title="Ambasse bey">ambasse bey</a> of the coast, <a href="/wiki/Assiko" title="Assiko">assiko</a> of the Bassa, <a href="/wiki/Mangambeu" title="Mangambeu">mangambeu</a> of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bamileke" title="Bamileke">Bangangte</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Tsamassi" title="Tsamassi">tsamassi</a> of the Bamileke.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-156"><a href="#cite_note-156">[156]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Nigeria" title="Music of Nigeria">Nigerian music</a> has influenced Anglophone Cameroonian performers, and <a href="/wiki/Prince_Nico_Mbarga" title="Prince Nico Mbarga">Prince Nico Mbarga</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Highlife" title="Highlife">highlife</a> hit "<a href="/wiki/Sweet_Mother" title="Sweet Mother">Sweet Mother</a>" is the top-selling African record in history.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-157"><a href="#cite_note-157">[157]</a></sup>
</p><p>The two most popular styles of music are <a href="/wiki/Makossa" title="Makossa">makossa</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bikutsi" title="Bikutsi">bikutsi</a>. Makossa developed in Douala and mixes folk music, highlife, <a href="/wiki/Soul_music" title="Soul music">soul</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Soukous" title="Soukous">Congo music</a>. Performers such as <a href="/wiki/Manu_Dibango" title="Manu Dibango">Manu Dibango</a>, <a href="/wiki/Francis_Bebey" title="Francis Bebey">Francis Bebey</a>, <a href="/wiki/Moni_Bil%C3%A9" title="Moni Bilé">Moni Bilé</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Petit-Pays" title="Petit-Pays">Petit-Pays</a> popularised the style worldwide in the 1970s and 1980s. Bikutsi originated as war music among the Ewondo. Artists such as <a href="/wiki/Anne-Marie_Nzi%C3%A9" title="Anne-Marie Nzié">Anne-Marie Nzié</a> developed it into a popular dance music beginning in the 1940s, and performers such as <a href="/wiki/Mama_Ohandja" title="Mama Ohandja">Mama Ohandja</a> and <a href="/wiki/Les_T%C3%AAtes_Brul%C3%A9es" title="Les Têtes Brulées">Les Têtes Brulées</a> popularised it internationally during the 1960s, 1970s, and 1980s.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-158"><a href="#cite_note-158">[158]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Nkolo_159-0"><a href="#cite_note-Nkolo-159">[159]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cuisine">Cuisine</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cameroon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Cuisine">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Cameroonian_cuisine" title="Cameroonian cuisine">Cameroonian cuisine</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Woman_weaving_baskets_near_Lake_Ossa.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1173" data-file-width="1485" height="174" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/Woman_weaving_baskets_near_Lake_Ossa.jpg/220px-Woman_weaving_baskets_near_Lake_Ossa.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/Woman_weaving_baskets_near_Lake_Ossa.jpg/330px-Woman_weaving_baskets_near_Lake_Ossa.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/Woman_weaving_baskets_near_Lake_Ossa.jpg/440px-Woman_weaving_baskets_near_Lake_Ossa.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Woman_weaving_baskets_near_Lake_Ossa.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A woman weaves a basket near <a href="/wiki/Lake_Ossa" title="Lake Ossa">Lake Ossa</a>, Littoral Region. Cameroonians practise such handicrafts throughout the country.</div></div></div>
<p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cuisine_of_Cameroon" title="Cuisine of Cameroon">Cuisine</a> varies by region, but a large, one-course, evening meal is common throughout the country. A typical dish is based on cocoyams, <a href="/wiki/Maize" title="Maize">maize</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cassava" title="Cassava">cassava</a> (manioc), <a href="/wiki/Millet" title="Millet">millet</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Plantain_(cooking)" title="Plantain (cooking)">plantains</a>, <a href="/wiki/Potato" title="Potato">potatoes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rice" title="Rice">rice</a>, or <a href="/wiki/Yam_(vegetable)" title="Yam (vegetable)">yams</a>, often pounded into dough-like <a href="/wiki/Fufu" title="Fufu">fufu</a>. This is served with a sauce, soup, or stew made from greens, <a href="/wiki/Groundnut" title="Groundnut">groundnuts</a>, <a href="/wiki/Palm_oil" title="Palm oil">palm oil</a>, or other ingredients.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-160"><a href="#cite_note-160">[160]</a></sup> Meat and fish are popular but expensive additions, with chicken often reserved for special occasions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mbaku_121-2_161-0"><a href="#cite_note-Mbaku_121-2-161">[161]</a></sup> Dishes are often quite hot, spiced with salt, red pepper sauce, and <a href="/wiki/Maggi" title="Maggi">Maggi</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-162"><a href="#cite_note-162">[162]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-163"><a href="#cite_note-163">[163]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-164"><a href="#cite_note-164">[164]</a></sup>
</p><p>Cutlery is common, but food is traditionally manipulated with the right hand. Breakfast consists of leftovers of bread and fruit with <a href="/wiki/Coffee" title="Coffee">coffee</a> or <a href="/wiki/Tea" title="Tea">tea</a>. Generally breakfast is made from wheat flour in various different foods such as puff-puff (doughnuts), accra banana made from <a href="/wiki/Banana" title="Banana">bananas</a> and flour, bean cakes and many more. Snacks are popular, especially in larger towns where they may be bought from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Street_vendor" title="Street vendor">street vendors</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-165"><a href="#cite_note-165">[165]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-166"><a href="#cite_note-166">[166]</a></sup>
</p><p>Water, <a href="/wiki/Palm_wine" title="Palm wine">palm wine</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Millet_beer" title="Millet beer">millet beer</a> are the traditional mealtime drinks, although beer, soda, and wine have gained popularity. 33 Export beer is the official drink of the <a href="/wiki/Cameroon_national_football_team" title="Cameroon national football team">national soccer team</a> and one of the most popular brands, joining Castel, <a href="/wiki/Amstel_Brewery" title="Amstel Brewery">Amstel Brewery</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Guinness_Foreign_Extra_Stout" title="Guinness Foreign Extra Stout">Guinness</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Local_arts_and_crafts">Local arts and crafts</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cameroon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Local arts and crafts">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Traditional arts and crafts are practiced throughout the country for commercial, decorative, and religious purposes. Woodcarvings and sculptures are especially common.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-167"><a href="#cite_note-167">[167]</a></sup> The high-quality clay of the western highlands is suitable for pottery and ceramics.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-West_18_151-2"><a href="#cite_note-West_18-151">[151]</a></sup> Other crafts include <a href="/wiki/Basket_weaving" title="Basket weaving">basket weaving</a>, beadworking, brass and bronze working, calabash carving and painting, embroidery, and leather working. Traditional housing styles make use of locally available materials and vary from temporary wood-and-leaf shelters of nomadic <a href="/wiki/Wodaabe" title="Wodaabe">Mbororo</a> to the rectangular mud-and-thatch homes of southern peoples. Dwellings made from materials such as cement and tin are increasingly common.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-168"><a href="#cite_note-168">[168]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Contemporary_art" title="Contemporary art">Contemporary art</a> is mainly promoted by independent cultural organizations (<a href="/wiki/Doual%27art" title="Doual'art">Doual'art</a>, <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Africr%C3%A9a&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Africréa (page does not exist)">Africréa</a>) and <a href="/wiki/Artist-run_initiative" title="Artist-run initiative">artist-run initiatives</a> (<a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Art_Wash&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Art Wash (page does not exist)">Art Wash</a>, <a href="/wiki/Atelier_Viking" title="Atelier Viking">Atelier Viking</a>, <a href="/wiki/ArtBakery" title="ArtBakery">ArtBakery</a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-169"><a href="#cite_note-169">[169]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Literature">Literature</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cameroon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Literature">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Literature_of_Cameroon" title="Literature of Cameroon">Literature of Cameroon</a></div>
<p>Cameroonian literature has concentrated on both European and African themes. Colonial-era writers such as <a href="/wiki/Louis-Marie_Pouka" title="Louis-Marie Pouka">Louis-Marie Pouka</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sankie_Maimo" title="Sankie Maimo">Sankie Maimo</a> were educated by European missionary societies and advocated <a href="/wiki/Cultural_assimilation" title="Cultural assimilation">assimilation</a> into European culture as the means to bring Cameroon into the modern world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-170"><a href="#cite_note-170">[170]</a></sup> After <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>, writers such as <a href="/wiki/Mongo_Beti" title="Mongo Beti">Mongo Beti</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ferdinand_Oyono" title="Ferdinand Oyono">Ferdinand Oyono</a> analysed and criticised colonialism and rejected assimilation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Fitzpatrick_171-0"><a href="#cite_note-Fitzpatrick-171">[171]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-172"><a href="#cite_note-172">[172]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Volet_173-0"><a href="#cite_note-Volet-173">[173]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Films_and_Literatures">Films and Literatures</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cameroon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Films and Literatures">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Cinema_of_Cameroon" title="Cinema of Cameroon">Cinema of Cameroon</a></div>
<p>Shortly after independence, filmmakers such as <a href="/wiki/Jean-Paul_Ngassa" title="Jean-Paul Ngassa">Jean-Paul Ngassa</a> and <a href="/wiki/Th%C3%A9r%C3%A8se_Sita-Bella" title="Thérèse Sita-Bella">Thérèse Sita-Bella</a> explored similar themes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-174"><a href="#cite_note-174">[174]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-175"><a href="#cite_note-175">[175]</a></sup> In the 1960s, <a href="/wiki/Mongo_Beti" title="Mongo Beti">Mongo Beti</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ferdinand_L%C3%A9opold_Oyono" title="Ferdinand Léopold Oyono">Ferdinand Léopold Oyono</a> and other writers explored post-colonialism, problems of African development, and the recovery of African identity.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-176"><a href="#cite_note-176">[176]</a></sup> Meanwhile, in the mid-1970s, filmmakers such as <a href="/wiki/Jean-Pierre_Dikongu%C3%A9_Pipa" title="Jean-Pierre Dikongué Pipa">Jean-Pierre Dikongué Pipa</a> and <a href="/wiki/Daniel_Kamwa" title="Daniel Kamwa">Daniel Kamwa</a> dealt with the conflicts between traditional and post-colonial society. Literature and films during the next two decades concentrated more on wholly Cameroonian themes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-177"><a href="#cite_note-177">[177]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cameroon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Sports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Sport_in_Cameroon" title="Sport in Cameroon">Sport in Cameroon</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Cameroon_vs_Germany_2003.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="581" data-file-width="731" height="238" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Cameroon_vs_Germany_2003.jpg/300px-Cameroon_vs_Germany_2003.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Cameroon_vs_Germany_2003.jpg/450px-Cameroon_vs_Germany_2003.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Cameroon_vs_Germany_2003.jpg/600px-Cameroon_vs_Germany_2003.jpg 2x" width="300"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Cameroon_vs_Germany_2003.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Cameroon_national_football_team" title="Cameroon national football team">Cameroon</a> faces <a href="/wiki/Germany_national_football_team" title="Germany national football team">Germany</a> at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Zentralstadion" title="Zentralstadion">Zentralstadion</a> in Leipzig, 17 November 2004.</div></div></div>
<p>National policy strongly advocates sport in all forms. Traditional sports include canoe racing and wrestling, and several hundred runners participate in the 40 km (25 mi) <a href="/wiki/Mount_Cameroon_Race_of_Hope" title="Mount Cameroon Race of Hope">Mount Cameroon Race of Hope</a> each year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-178"><a href="#cite_note-178">[178]</a></sup> Cameroon is one of the few tropical countries to have <a href="/wiki/Cameroon_at_the_2002_Winter_Olympics" title="Cameroon at the 2002 Winter Olympics">competed</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Winter_Olympic_Games" title="Winter Olympic Games">Winter Olympics</a>.
</p><p>Sport in Cameroon is dominated by football. Amateur football clubs abound, organised along ethnic lines or under corporate sponsors. The <a href="/wiki/Cameroon_national_football_team" title="Cameroon national football team">national team</a> has been one of the most successful in Africa since its strong showing in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1982_Football_World_Cup" title="1982 Football World Cup">1982</a> and <a href="/wiki/1990_FIFA_World_Cup" title="1990 FIFA World Cup">1990 FIFA World Cups</a>. Cameroon has won five <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/African_Cup_of_Nations" title="African Cup of Nations">African Cup of Nations</a> titles and the gold medal at the <a href="/wiki/Football_at_the_2000_Summer_Olympics_%E2%80%93_Men%27s_tournament" title="Football at the 2000 Summer Olympics – Men's tournament">2000 Olympics</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-179"><a href="#cite_note-179">[179]</a></sup>
</p><p>Cameroon was the host country of the <a href="/wiki/Africa_Women_Cup_of_Nations" title="Africa Women Cup of Nations">Women Africa Cup of Nations</a> in November–December 2016.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-180"><a href="#cite_note-180">[180]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Cameroon_women%27s_national_football_team" title="Cameroon women's national football team">women's football team</a> is known as the "Indomitable Lionesses." 
</p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Human_Rights">Human Rights</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cameroon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Human Rights">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The Office of the <a href="/wiki/Office_of_the_United_Nations_High_Commissioner_for_Human_Rights" title="Office of the United Nations High Commissioner for Human Rights">United Nations High Commissioner for Human Rights</a> reports that Cameroon Government forces are responsible for killings, the excessive use of force, burning down of houses, arbitrary detentions and torture. UN figures indicate that more than 21,000 people have fled to neighboring countries, while 160,000 have been internally displaced by the violence, many reportedly hiding in forests.
On 25 July 2018,  UN High Commissioner for Human Rights <a href="/wiki/Zeid_Raad_Al_Hussein" title="Zeid Raad Al Hussein">Zeid Ra’ad Al Hussein</a> expressed deep concern about reports of violations and abuses in the English-speaking Northwest and Southwest regions of Cameroon.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-181"><a href="#cite_note-181">[181]</a></sup>
</p>
